<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;color:darkslategray; font-size:smaller;">Updated on 18 March 2012.</td>

<p><b>Magdalena "Lena" Neuner</b> (since her 2014 marriage legally <i>Magdalena Holzer</i>, born 9 February 1987) is a retired <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">German</a> professional <a href="/wiki/Biathlon" title="Biathlon">biathlete</a>. She is the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships#Multiple_medallist" title="Biathlon World Championships">most successful woman of all time</a> at <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships" title="Biathlon World Championships">Biathlon World Championships</a> and a two-time Olympic gold medalist. At the age of 21, she became the youngest Overall World Cup winner in the history of the <a href="/wiki/International_Biathlon_Union" title="International Biathlon Union">International Biathlon Union</a> (IBU). With 34 World Cup wins, Neuner is ranked second all-time for career victories on the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Cup" title="Biathlon World Cup">Biathlon World Cup</a> tour. She has won the Overall World Cup title three times, in <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2007–08 Biathlon World Cup">2007–08</a>, in <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2009–10 Biathlon World Cup">2009–10</a> and her final season in <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2011–12 Biathlon World Cup">2011–12</a>. Neuner retired from the sport in March 2012, citing a lack of motivation and her desire for a normal life.</p>
<p>Neuner started biathlon when she was nine years old and won five junior world championship titles from 2004 to 2006. She made her World Cup debut in 2006 and won her first World Cup race in January 2007. One month later, she claimed three gold medals in her <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2007" title="Biathlon World Championships 2007">first appearance</a> at the Biathlon World Championships. In the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2007–08 Biathlon World Cup">2007–08 season</a>, Neuner won the Overall World Cup and once more claimed three titles at the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2008" title="Biathlon World Championships 2008">2008 World Championships</a>. After a less successful winter in <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2008–09 Biathlon World Cup">2008–09</a>, she participated in her first <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">Winter Olympic Games</a> in 2010, winning the gold medal in both the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_pursuit" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics – Women's pursuit">pursuit</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_mass_start" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics – Women's mass start">mass start</a>, and silver in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_sprint" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics – Women's sprint">sprint race</a>. Neuner also claimed the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2009–10 Biathlon World Cup">2009–10 Overall World Cup</a> title. At the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2011" title="Biathlon World Championships 2011">2011 World Championships</a>, she won three more gold medals. In her final winter on the World Cup tour, Neuner won two more titles at the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2012" title="Biathlon World Championships 2012">2012 World Championships</a> and claimed the Overall World Cup for a third time.</p>
<p>During her seven World Cup seasons, Neuner won 34 World Cup races and achieved 63 podium finishes. As part of Germany's World Cup team, she won ten relay races and three mixed relay events. During six appearances at Biathlon World Championships, Neuner claimed 17 medals: twelve gold, four silver and one bronze. In addition, she has won seven junior world championship titles. Neuner was known as one of the fastest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cross-country_skier" title="Cross-country skier">cross-country skiers</a> in biathlon. She had been noted for her volatile shooting performances in the standing position, particularly in the early years of her career, often at the expense of better results.</p>
<p>Neuner has lived in the <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavarian</a> village of <a href="/wiki/Wallgau" title="Wallgau">Wallgau</a> since birth. At the age of 16, she joined the <a href="/wiki/Bundeszollverwaltung" title="Bundeszollverwaltung">German Customs Administration</a> to become a member of the government-funded Customs-Ski-Team. Since winning three world championship gold medals in 2007, Neuner is one of her home country's most popular female athletes. She was named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Sportspersonality_of_the_year" title="German Sportspersonality of the year">German Sportswoman of the Year</a> in 2007, 2011 and 2012.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Magdalena Neuner was born in the German alpine resort town of <a href="/wiki/Garmisch-Partenkirchen" title="Garmisch-Partenkirchen">Garmisch-Partenkirchen</a>, the second of four children of bank clerk Paul Neuner and his wife Margit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parents_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-parents-2">[2]</a></sup> She has an elder brother Paul, and two younger siblings—her brother Christoph and her sister Anna. Her sister is also an aspiring biathlete who participates in junior competitions and is a member in the youth squad of the Bavarian Ski Association.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BSV_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-BSV-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Neuner grew up in the small <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavarian</a> village of <a href="/wiki/Wallgau" title="Wallgau">Wallgau</a>, approximately 15 kilometres (9.3 mi) from Garmisch-Partenkirchen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-encarta_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-encarta-4">[4]</a></sup> She started <a href="/wiki/Alpine_skiing" title="Alpine skiing">alpine skiing</a> when she was four years old and later tried various other winter sports at her hometown ski club SC Wallgau.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parents_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-parents-2">[2]</a></sup> At the age of 16, Neuner finished high school (<i><a href="/wiki/Realschule" title="Realschule">Realschule</a></i>) in Garmisch-Partenkirchen and decided to pursue a career in biathlon. Her parents were reluctant, but they eventually supported her ambition to become a professional biathlete.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spiegel_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-spiegel-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career_and_World_Cup_debut">Early career and World Cup debut</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early career and World Cup debut">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Neuner started biathlon when she was nine years old after she had participated in a try out course at her local ski club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-6">[6]</a></sup> She won 29 races at the biathlon Student's Cup of the <a href="/wiki/German_Ski_Association" title="German Ski Association">German Ski Association</a> (DSV),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BSV_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-BSV-3">[3]</a></sup> claiming the overall title in her respective age-group for four years in a row from 1999 to 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parents_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-parents-2">[2]</a></sup> After finishing school, Neuner joined the <a href="/wiki/Bundeszollverwaltung" title="Bundeszollverwaltung">German Customs Administration</a> in August 2003 to become a member in the government-supported Customs-Ski-Team (<i>Zoll-Ski-Team</i>). She officially holds the rank of <i>Erste Zollhauptwachtmeisterin</i> (first head customs officer),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-finmin_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-finmin-7">[7]</a></sup> although she is a full-time professional athlete with no customs obligations. One of her team mates is alpine skiing world champion <a href="/wiki/Maria_H%C3%B6fl-Riesch" title="Maria Höfl-Riesch">Maria Höfl-Riesch</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2003, Neuner won the German Cup for 17-year-olds, which led to her appointment for the 2003–04 European Cup competition for juniors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-encarta_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-encarta-4">[4]</a></sup> With four wins at European level, Neuner qualified for the 2004 Junior/Youth World Championships in <a href="/wiki/Maurienne" title="Maurienne">Haute Maurienne</a>, France, where she won the sprint and relay events, as well as silver in the pursuit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-encarta_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-encarta-4">[4]</a></sup> One year later at the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_Junior_World_Championships_2005" title="Biathlon Junior World Championships 2005">2005 Junior/Youth World Championships</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kontiolahti" title="Kontiolahti">Kontiolahti</a>, Finland, she claimed two silver medals (pursuit and relay), and again won the sprint discipline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-6"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup> With her success at junior level, Neuner at 18 years old, was considered one of Germany's biggest biathlon talents ever. Even before achieving any results at senior level, she had signed a sponsorship deal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Magdalena_Neuner.jpg"><img alt="A young woman in multicoloured winter sportswear and with the number 19 on her jersey smiles into the camera, standing in a field covered with snow. <tr>
<td colspan="9" style="text-align:center;"><small style="line-height:130%"><i>Key:"—" denotes discipline not held; DNS—Did not start</i></small><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-7"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2005–06 Biathlon World Cup">2005–06 season</a>, Neuner made her first appearances in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Cup" title="Biathlon World Cup">Biathlon World Cup</a>. Germany's women's national coach Uwe Müßiggang had already considered her for the team two years earlier, however, her parents and her hometown coaches Bernhard Kröll and Herbert Mayer were reluctant to let her start prematurely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parents_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-parents-2">[2]</a></sup> On 13 January 2006, Neuner made her debut in the World Cup sprint race in <a href="/wiki/Ruhpolding" title="Ruhpolding">Ruhpolding</a>, Germany, where she substituted for the injured <a href="/wiki/Uschi_Disl" title="Uschi Disl">Uschi Disl</a>. Although her first appearance ended unsuccessfully, coming in 41st place,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> she was appointed for nine more World Cup races for the remainder of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-8"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Neuner returned as one of the favourites at the 2006 Junior/Youth World Championships in <a href="/wiki/Presque_Isle,_Maine" title="Presque Isle, Maine">Presque Isle, Maine</a>, United States, where she won two more titles (pursuit and relay) in addition to a silver medal in the sprint race.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-9"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup> She did not participate in the <a href="/wiki/2006_Winter_Olympics" title="2006 Winter Olympics">2006 Winter Olympics</a> for the German team. At the World Cup in Kontiolahti in March 2006, Neuner achieved her first top ten finishes: she was fourth in the sprint and came in ninth in the mass start race.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Three_world_championship_titles_.282006.E2.80.9307_season.29">Three world championship titles (2006–07 season)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Three world championship titles (2006–07 season)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>While she had only competed in ten races during her first World Cup winter, Neuner became a fixture in the German team in the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2006–07 Biathlon World Cup">2006–07 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-encarta_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-encarta-4">[4]</a></sup> She proved to be one of the fastest <a href="/wiki/Cross-country_skiing" title="Cross-country skiing">cross-country skiers</a> in biathlon, and at 19 years old, regularly set the fastest course times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kicker_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-kicker-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="ref_skiinga"><a href="#endnote_skiinga">[note a]</a></sup> On 5 January 2007, Neuner won her first World Cup event, the sprint race in <a href="/wiki/Oberhof,_Germany" title="Oberhof, Germany">Oberhof</a>, Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Her victory on home soil, before a crowd of 19,000 people, received considerable media attention and put her into the national spotlight for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Two days later at the pursuit race, she forgot to reload her rifle after warm-up. She was handed a new magazine during the prone shooting and managed to finish third despite a total of six <a href="/wiki/Shooting_errors" title="Shooting errors">shooting errors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Neuner was scheduled to compete at the junior world championships in 2007. However, following her first World Cup win, she was instead appointed for the senior <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2007" title="Biathlon World Championships 2007">World Championships</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rasen-Antholz" title="Rasen-Antholz">Antholz</a>, Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-encarta_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-encarta-4">[4]</a></sup> On 3 February 2007, she won gold in the sprint, beating <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anna_Carin_Olofsson" title="Anna Carin Olofsson">Anna Carin Olofsson</a> by 2.3 seconds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> It was her first world championship event ever and only her second victory at senior level.<sup class="reference" id="ref_WCHb"><a href="#endnote_WCHb">[note b]</a></sup> One day later, she also claimed the pursuit title, in spite of four shooting errors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wc2_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-wc2-18">[18]</a></sup> Following a 14th place in the mass start, Neuner, alongside <a href="/wiki/Martina_Beck" title="Martina Beck">Martina Beck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Henkel" title="Andrea Henkel">Andrea Henkel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kati_Wilhelm" title="Kati Wilhelm">Kati Wilhelm</a>, also won gold in the relay race on 11 February 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> With three titles, she was the championship's most successful athlete and became the youngest triple world champion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the end of the season, she continued her successful run with four more World Cup wins. In March 2007, Neuner won the pursuit and mass start races at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holmenkollen_ski_jump" title="Holmenkollen ski jump">Holmenkollen</a> in Oslo, Norway,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> and she won the sprint and pursuit events at the season final in <a href="/wiki/Khanty-Mansiysk" title="Khanty-Mansiysk">Khanty-Mansiysk</a>, Russia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cup6_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-cup6-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> giving her seven career World Cup wins. She ended her first complete season fourth in the Overall World Cup standings and finished second in the pursuit discipline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-11"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup> In the course of three months, Neuner had emerged from anonymity to become one of Germany's most popular female athletes. At the end of 2007, she had earned an estimated 1.3 million euros through sponsorship and endorsement deals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-focus_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-focus-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overall_World_Cup_winner_.282007.E2.80.9308_season.29">Overall World Cup winner (2007–08 season)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Overall World Cup winner (2007–08 season)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Neuner-Oslo08-1.jpg"><img alt="A woman cross country skis uphill towards the camera, holding a red ski pole in each hand. A second skier behind her can be seen on the left." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3435" data-file-width="2290" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Neuner-Oslo08-1.jpg/170px-Neuner-Oslo08-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Neuner-Oslo08-1.jpg/255px-Neuner-Oslo08-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Neuner-Oslo08-1.jpg/340px-Neuner-Oslo08-1.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Neuner-Oslo08-1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Neuner in the yellow bib of the Overall World Cup leader, March 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After missing the podium at the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2007–08 Biathlon World Cup">2007–08 season</a>'s first two World Cups, Neuner was part of Germany's winning relay team in <a href="/wiki/Pokljuka" title="Pokljuka">Pokljuka</a>, Slovenia in December 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> She claimed her eighth World Cup win at the mass start in Oberhof in January 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> and later that month won the relay race in Ruhpolding with the German team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Shortly before her 21st birthday, Neuner decided to again compete at the Junior/Youth World Championships, held in Ruhpolding in January 2008—the last time she was eligible to enter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-handbook_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-handbook-28">[28]</a></sup> She won gold in the sprint and the pursuit, but withdrew from the individual race to prepare for the senior world championships alongside her German team mates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-13"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Leading up to the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2008" title="Biathlon World Championships 2008">2008 World Championships</a> in <a href="/wiki/%C3%96stersund" title="Östersund">Östersund</a>, Sweden, Neuner tried to lower expectations, stating a repeat of last year's performance would be impossible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> She failed to defend her titles in the sprint and pursuit races, with shooting errors preventing better results; she finished 17th and sixth respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-14"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup> On 12 February 2008, she won the mixed relay with <a href="/wiki/Sabrina_Buchholz" title="Sabrina Buchholz">Sabrina Buchholz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andreas_Birnbacher" title="Andreas Birnbacher">Andreas Birnbacher</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Greis" title="Michael Greis">Michael Greis</a> to claim her first gold medal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Four days later, she won her second title in the mass start, beating Norway's <a href="/wiki/Tora_Berger" title="Tora Berger">Tora Berger</a> by 3.0 seconds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wc5_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-wc5-31">[31]</a></sup> She had four shooting errors compared to Berger's one and skied side by side with the Norwegian for most of the last lap, in what she later described as her hardest fought victory ever.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Alongside Martina Beck, Andrea Henkel and Kati Wilhelm, Neuner also claimed gold in the relay race on 17 February 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> By winning three more titles, she became the youngest six-time world champion, solidifying her status as Germany's biggest biathlon star.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the following World Cups, she won the sprint races in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pyeongchang" title="Pyeongchang">Pyeongchang</a>, South Korea, and in Khanty-Mansiysk—her tenth and eleventh World Cup victories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> With a second-place finish in the penultimate mass start race of the season, Neuner won the 2007–08 Mass start World Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> At the season final in Oslo, she also claimed the season's Sprint World Cup and took over the yellow bib of the Overall World Cup leader for the first time in her career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> In the last race of the season, a ninth place in the mass start ensured Neuner the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2007–08 Biathlon World Cup">2007–08 Overall Biathlon World Cup</a> victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> She was the youngest Overall World Cup winner since the <a href="/wiki/International_Biathlon_Union" title="International Biathlon Union">International Biathlon Union</a> was established in 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="ref_winnerc"><a href="#endnote_winnerc">[note c]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_setbacks_.282008.E2.80.9309_season.29">First setbacks (2008–09 season)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: First setbacks (2008–09 season)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed" style="font-size:90%; text-align:center; float:left; margin:1em 1em 1em 0;">
<tr>
<th colspan="9" style="white-space:nowrap; text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2008–09 Biathlon World Cup">2008–09 World Cup season</a> results  </th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th><small>No.</small></th>
<th><small>World Cup location</small></th>
<td rowspan="11" style="border-bottom-width:2x; padding:0;"></td>
<th><small>Individual</small></th>
<th><small>Sprint</small></th>
<th><small>Pursuit</small></th>
<th><small>Mass start</small></th>
<th><small>Relay</small></th>
<th><small>Mixed relay</small></th>
</tr>

<td colspan="9" style="text-align:center;"><small style="line-height:130%"><i>Key:"—" denotes discipline not held; DNS—Did not start; WCH—World Championships</i></small><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-15"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></td>

<p>Neuner's preparation for the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2008–09 Biathlon World Cup">2008–09 season</a> was affected by several illnesses. In the summer, she battled an intestinal fungus which forced her to pause training for seven weeks;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> she later attributed it to pressure of public expectations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pleiten_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-pleiten-42">[42]</a></sup> In October 2008, she contracted influenza and in November, a bacterial infection caused her to miss two weeks of training.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Subsequently, her ski speed saw a substantial drop at the start of the season. In the first four World Cups, Neuner only achieved two individual podiums; atypically courtesy of good shooting performances, not her skiing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.C3.B6stersund_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-.C3.B6stersund-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Neuner-Antholz09-3.png"><img alt="A woman on cross country skies wearing a red cap, a white jersey with the number 15 and black trousers skies away from a shooting range covered in snow. Half a dozen people in the background are shooting while lying on the ground." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="969" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Neuner-Antholz09-3.png/220px-Neuner-Antholz09-3.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Neuner-Antholz09-3.png/330px-Neuner-Antholz09-3.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Neuner-Antholz09-3.png/440px-Neuner-Antholz09-3.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Neuner-Antholz09-3.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Neuner leaves the shooting range at the World Cup in <a href="/wiki/Rasen-Antholz" title="Rasen-Antholz">Antholz</a>, January 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the Christmas break, her skiing times had improved. In Ruhpolding in January 2009, Neuner was part of the winning German relay team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> She beat team mate Kati Wilhelm by 0.2 seconds in the Ruhpolding sprint and also won the following pursuit event, which marked her World Cup wins twelve and thirteen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cup13_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-cup13-48">[48]</a></sup> Neuner again missed the podium in Antholz. She was leading the mass start by 53.6 seconds before the final shooting, in which she missed all five targets, eventually finishing sixth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disaster_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-disaster-49">[49]</a></sup> This result received much public attention. She later described it as a pivotal moment in her career and called it the "total end of the world".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>Neuner suffered further setbacks at the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2009" title="Biathlon World Championships 2009">2009 World Championships</a> in Pyeongchang, where she struggled with a cold and a high number of shooting errors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> She finished eighth in the sprint, in which she crashed on a downhill slope,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> and came in eleventh in the pursuit race.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> She was not appointed for the individual race and could not start in the mixed relay due to her cold. On 21 February 2009, Neuner claimed silver as part Germany's women's relay team, alongside Martina Beck, Andrea Henkel and Kati Wilhelm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> On the last day of the championships, she came in seventh in the mass start race.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the Olympic rehearsal in <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>, Canada, in March 2009, Neuner claimed the 2008–09 Individual World Cup, despite never having won a race in that discipline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> She also won the Vancouver relay race with the German team,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> and was second in the sprint, 0.7 seconds behind Sweden's <a href="/wiki/Helena_Ekholm" title="Helena Ekholm">Helena Ekholm</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> At the season final in Khanty-Mansiysk, Neuner won the pursuit race—her 14th World Cup win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> She ended the season fourth in the Overall Biathlon World Cup,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-16"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup> which was generally considered disappointing in the media.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Neuner later revealed that due to public expectations and constant media attention, the 2008–09 season had been extremely difficult for her psychologically, and she even briefly contemplated retirement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> She started working with a psychologist and cut down her media appearances as much as possible in the summer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSJ_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Double_Olympic_champion_.282009.E2.80.9310_season.29">Double Olympic champion (2009–10 season)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Double Olympic champion (2009–10 season)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>Neuner competed at the Summer Biathlon World Championships for the first time in September 2009 when they were held in Oberhof. She only reluctantly agreed to interrupt training and participate in the summer event, which is contested on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roller_ski" title="Roller ski">roller ski</a>, however she went on to win gold in all three competitions (sprint, pursuit and mixed relay).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Neuner missed the first World Cup of the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2009–10 Biathlon World Cup">2009–10 season</a> due to a cold in December 2009. She returned at the following races in Hochfilzen, but was still affected by her cold and finished outside the top 20. Her first podiums of the winter came in Pokljuka, finishing third in the sprint and second in the pursuit race.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Thereby she secured her Olympic qualification within the German team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Neuner-Vancouver-MassStart-cropped.jpg"><img alt=" A woman in multicoloured winter sportswear which features the Olympic rings on her cheast and the number 2 in the center, moves twoards the camera. She is pictured in an area covered in snow. A second person can be seen in the background to her right. An out of focus red-and-white flag covers the upper parts of the image." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1248" data-file-width="2014" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Neuner-Vancouver-MassStart-cropped.jpg/220px-Neuner-Vancouver-MassStart-cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Neuner-Vancouver-MassStart-cropped.jpg/330px-Neuner-Vancouver-MassStart-cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Neuner-Vancouver-MassStart-cropped.jpg/440px-Neuner-Vancouver-MassStart-cropped.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Neuner-Vancouver-MassStart-cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Neuner shortly before crossing the finish line during the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_mass_start" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics – Women's mass start">Olympic mass start race</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Shortly before the Oberhof sprint in January 2010, Neuner injured her back during warm-up and had to withdraw.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> She returned in Ruhpolding where she came in third in both the sprint and the mass start race.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> In her first relay of the season, she dealt a blow to the German team by incurring two penalty loops, with Germany finishing fourth eventually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> With some top competitors missing in Antholz at the last World Cup before the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a>, Neuner won two events—the first individual race of her career as well as the sprint, giving her 16 career World Cup wins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wc14_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-wc14-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> She also came in second in the pursuit, which marked her seventh consecutive podium finish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>Neuner went into her first Winter Olympics in Vancouver with the declared aim of winning a gold medal. On 13 February 2010, she participated in the opening <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_sprint" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics – Women's sprint">sprint</a>, which was contested at <a href="/wiki/Whistler_Olympic_Park" title="Whistler Olympic Park">Whistler Olympic Park</a> in rainy conditions. With one shooting error, Neuner claimed the silver medal, finishing 1.5 seconds behind <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Anastasiya_Kuzmina" title="Anastasiya Kuzmina">Anastasiya Kuzmina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> She uncharacteristically lost five seconds against the unheralded Slovak on the cross-country course, which led to speculation of inferior ski preparation in the German media.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Three days later, Neuner won gold in the subsequent <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_pursuit" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics – Women's pursuit">pursuit race</a>. Despite missing two targets in the standing position, she beat sprint winner Kuzmina by 12.3 seconds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> In her third Olympic event, she finished tenth in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_individual" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics – Women's individual">individual</a>. She had three shooting mistakes and said it had been difficult for her to immediately get her concentration back after winning her first gold medal. On 21 February 2010, Neuner claimed her second gold of the Games in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_mass_start" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics – Women's mass start">mass start</a>. After missing two targets, she had been trailing by as much as 29 seconds, but she pushed the pace and a clean final standing shoot allowed her to overtake Russia's <a href="/wiki/Olga_Zaitseva" title="Olga Zaitseva">Olga Zaitseva</a> on the last lap.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> After the race, Neuner made the announcement not to participate in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_relay" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics – Women's relay">relay</a>, citing mental exhaustion and her desire to give all of her team mates the chance to win a medal. Her withdrawal allowed her friend <a href="/wiki/Martina_Beck" title="Martina Beck">Martina Beck</a> a start in her last Olympic Games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-77">[77]</a></sup> Neuner was Germany's most successful athlete in Vancouver and was chosen to carry the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_flag" title="German flag">German flag</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics_closing_ceremony" title="2010 Winter Olympics closing ceremony">closing ceremony</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following her Olympic success, Neuner continued her good form at the season's remaining three World Cups, finishing all races in the top ten. She came in second in the Kontiolahti pursuit,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> and third in Oslo's mass start race,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> which increased her World Cup lead after taking over the yellow bib in Vancouver. Neuner ended the season with her 19th World Cup win in Khanty-Mansiysk's mass start,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> which ensured her the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Biathlon_World_Cup_%E2%80%93_Overall_Women" title="2009–10 Biathlon World Cup – Overall Women">2009–10 Overall World Cup</a>, making her the first German woman to win the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Cup" title="Biathlon World Cup">Biathlon World Cup</a> for a second time. She also won the pursuit and mass start discipline World Cups. In the last event of the winter, the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2010" title="Biathlon World Championships 2010">Mixed Relay World Championship</a>, she won gold, alongside <a href="/wiki/Simone_Hauswald" title="Simone Hauswald">Simone Hauswald</a>, <a href="/wiki/Simon_Schempp" title="Simon Schempp">Simon Schempp</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arnd_Peiffer" title="Arnd Peiffer">Arnd Peiffer</a>, to claim her seventh world title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Record_world_champion_.282010.E2.80.9311_season.29">Record world champion (2010–11 season)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Record world champion (2010–11 season)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

</tr>
</table>
<p>During the summer, Neuner admitted struggling for motivation for the upcoming season, having won every title in the sport at only 23 years old. However, she vowed to continue her career at least until the 2012 world championships in Ruhpolding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> In December 2010 she suffered from a cold, missing the season's first World Cup in Östersund for the second year in a row. She started the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2010–11 Biathlon World Cup">2010–11 season</a> in Hochfilzen, where she managed two seventh-place finishes, and was part of the winning German relay team. At the third stop of the season in Pokljuka, she won the sprint race in spite of two shooting errors, claiming her 20th career victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Magdalena_Neuner_Wallgau_2011.jpg"><img alt="A blonde woman, wearing a predominately black jacket and blue jeans, stands in front of a large poster of a winter landscape, smiles and looks to the right. She holds a microphone in her right hand and several gold medals in her left hand." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2825" data-file-width="2120" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Magdalena_Neuner_Wallgau_2011.jpg/170px-Magdalena_Neuner_Wallgau_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Magdalena_Neuner_Wallgau_2011.jpg/255px-Magdalena_Neuner_Wallgau_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Magdalena_Neuner_Wallgau_2011.jpg/340px-Magdalena_Neuner_Wallgau_2011.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Magdalena_Neuner_Wallgau_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Neuner with her ten <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships" title="Biathlon World Championships">Biathlon World Championships</a> gold medals</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Neuner continued the winter with mixed results in January 2011. She reached the podium in the sprints of Oberhof and Ruhpolding, coming in second and third respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> In the relay in Oberhof, Neuner was part of Germany's team coming in sixth place, the team's worst result since 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> She also had her worst personal result in 13 months, finishing in 16th place in the Ruhpolding individual race, which ended her streak of 24 consecutive top ten finishes (including 15 podiums and 6 wins).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> At the World Cup in Antholz, Neuner again struggled with illness. She only participated in the concluding mass start, coming in 6th place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the World Cup stops in February in the United States, Neuner returned to good health and showed more consistency; her worst result was a 6th-place finish. In <a href="/wiki/Presque_Isle,_Maine" title="Presque Isle, Maine">Presque Isle, Maine</a>, she won the mixed relay as part of the German team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> On week later in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Kent,_Maine" title="Fort Kent, Maine">Fort Kent, Maine</a>, Neuner finished all three races on the podium. She came in third in the sprint,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> second in the pursuit,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> and claimed her 21st World Cup win in the mass start—the last race before the world championships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2011" title="Biathlon World Championships 2011">2011 World Championships</a> in Khanty-Mansiysk, Neuner won three gold and two silver medals. She claimed silver, alongside Andrea Henkel, Arnd Peiffer and Michael Greis, in the opening <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2011_%E2%80%93_Mixed_relay" title="Biathlon World Championships 2011 – Mixed relay">mixed relay</a>. On 5 March 2011, Neuner won the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2011_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_sprint" title="Biathlon World Championships 2011 – Women's sprint">sprint race</a> courtesy of a clean shooting performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> She finished second in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2011_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_pursuit" title="Biathlon World Championships 2011 – Women's pursuit">pursuit</a> and fifth in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2011_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_individual" title="Biathlon World Championships 2011 – Women's individual">individual</a> subsequently. On 12 March 2011, Neuner won her second title in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2011_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_mass_start" title="Biathlon World Championships 2011 – Women's mass start">mass start</a> despite of four shooing errors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> The following day she also claimed gold in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2011_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_relay" title="Biathlon World Championships 2011 – Women's relay">women's relay</a>, together with Andrea Henkel, <a href="/wiki/Miriam_G%C3%B6ssner" title="Miriam Gössner">Miriam Gössner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tina_Bachmann" title="Tina Bachmann">Tina Bachmann</a>. Running the last leg for Germany, Neuner started in fourth, 67.5 seconds off the lead, but she pulled back the entire time and moved in front on the last lap.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Her five medals made her the most successful female athlete in the history of <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships" title="Biathlon World Championships">Biathlon World Championships</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goldrausch_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-goldrausch-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>The season ended in disappointment for Neuner in Oslo. After claiming her 24th career win in the sprint, she had moved into second place in the Overall World Cup ranking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> However, she again suffered from a cold and had to pull out of the penultimate race of the winter, the pursuit in which she would have started 31 seconds in front. This effectively ended her hopes of retaining the World Cup crown. She eventually finished fifth in the overall standings, having missed five of the season's 26 races.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-19"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_World_Cup_winter_.282011.E2.80.9312_season.29">Final World Cup winter (2011–12 season)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Final World Cup winter (2011–12 season)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>Before the start of the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2011–12 Biathlon World Cup">2011–12 season</a>, Neuner hinted the upcoming season might be her last. She began the winter in Östersund with the best season start of her career, beating Tora Berger by 0.2 seconds in the sprint to claim her 25th World Cup win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> She also came third in the individual and the pursuit, and took the yellow bib of the Overall World Cup leader. On 6 December 2011, Neuner announced her retirement from biathlon by the end of the season on her homepage. She explained her early departure from the sport (at age 25) with a lack of motivation and her desire for a normal life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nach_dieser_Saison_ist_Schluss.21_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nach_dieser_Saison_ist_Schluss.21-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Neuner nonetheless continued her good form in Hochfilzen, where she claimed her 26th World Cup win in the sprint.</p>
<p>After Christmas, Neuner won both individual races in Oberhof – her World Cup wins 27 and 28.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> In the women’s relay, she incurred 4 penalties in the final shooting, which foiled a likely German victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> Neuner suffered one of the biggest mishaps of her career, when she fired on the wrong targets in the Nove Mesto pursuit, dropping from first to seventh place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> She recovered quickly by winning the sprint race in Antholz one week later. In February, Neuner claimed a double sprint and pursuit victory in Oslo despite suffering from a cold, which forced her to withdraw from the mass start. At the last World Cup stop before the world championships in Kontiolahti, she reached her sixth sprint win of the season, and extended her World Cup lead over <a href="/wiki/Darya_Domracheva" title="Darya Domracheva">Darya Domracheva</a>.</p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2012" title="Biathlon World Championships 2012">2012 World Championships</a> in Ruhpolding, Neuner won bronze in the opening <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2012_%E2%80%93_Mixed_relay" title="Biathlon World Championships 2012 – Mixed relay">mixed relay</a>, alongside Andrea Henkel, Andreas Birnbacher and Arnd Peiffer. On 3 March 2012, she claimed her 11th world title in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2012_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_sprint" title="Biathlon World Championships 2012 – Women's sprint">sprint race</a> courtesy of her clean shooting. Neuner dropped to second place one day later in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2012_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_pursuit" title="Biathlon World Championships 2012 – Women's pursuit">pursuit</a>, in which Domracheva overtook her at the final shooting bout. During the second week of the championships, Neuner often struggled with her shooting. She only reached 23rd place in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2012_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_individual" title="Biathlon World Championships 2012 – Women's individual">individual</a> – her worst world championships result ever. With Tina Bachmann, Miriam Gössner and Andrea Henkel she won her second gold medal in Ruhpolding in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2012_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_relay" title="Biathlon World Championships 2012 – Women's relay">women's relay</a> on 10 March 2012, despite incurring a penalty loop. In the concluding <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2012_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_mass_start" title="Biathlon World Championships 2012 – Women's mass start">mass start</a>, Neuner came in tenth place, with six shooting mistakes in total. Her 12th gold medal made her the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships#Multiple_medallist" title="Biathlon World Championships">second most successful biathlete of all time at world championships</a>, behind male record holder <a href="/wiki/Ole_Einar_Bj%C3%B8rndalen" title="Ole Einar Bjørndalen">Ole Einar Bjørndalen</a>.</p>
<p>Having led the standings uninterruptedly since the second race of the winter, Neuner won her third Overall World Cup title at the season final in Russia, where she claimed her 34th and final World Cup win in the sprint. Neuner also won the 2011–12 Sprint World Cup thanks to an unprecedented eight out of ten sprint wins. With ten victories in total, her final World Cup season was the most successful in her career. She also became only the second woman after <a href="/wiki/Magdalena_Forsberg" title="Magdalena Forsberg">Magdalena Forsberg</a> to win the overall title more than twice. On 18 March 2012, Neuner ended her biathlon career with a sixth place in the Khanty-Mansiysk mass start.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Skiing">Skiing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Skiing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Neuner-Trondheim09_-2.jpg"><img alt="A woman in predominantly black winter sportswear, wearing a red cap and a bright red jersey with the number 13, is pictured in a forested area covered with snow. She leans slightly forward and holds ski poles in her hands. There is a green conifer tree behind her and a second person can be seen in the background out of focus on the right." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Neuner-Trondheim09_-2.jpg/220px-Neuner-Trondheim09_-2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Neuner-Trondheim09_-2.jpg/330px-Neuner-Trondheim09_-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Neuner-Trondheim09_-2.jpg/440px-Neuner-Trondheim09_-2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Neuner-Trondheim09_-2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Neuner skies uphill at a World Cup race in <a href="/wiki/Trondheim" title="Trondheim">Trondheim</a>, March 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Neuner was one of the fastest female <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cross-country_skier" title="Cross-country skier">cross-country skiers</a> in biathlon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> During 66 of her 151 World Cup races (44%), she has set the fastest course time (race time without time spent at the shooting range or in the penalty loop).<sup class="reference" id="ref_skiingf"><a href="#endnote_skiingf">[note a]</a></sup> In addition, she has been among the top three fastest skiers in 77% of her career races.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-21"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>In her first World Cup races in the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2005–06 Biathlon World Cup">2005–06 season</a>, Neuner achieved average course times; her best result was being fourth fastest in the pursuit race in Kontiolahti.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> During her first full season in <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2006–07 Biathlon World Cup">2006–07</a>, she finished among the top three fastest skiers in 19 of her 24 races and came in fastest in seven of them. Neuner won the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2007–08 Biathlon World Cup">2007–08 Biathlon World Cup</a> with dominating skiing performances. She set the fastest course time in 19 of her 25 races and was second or third fastest in the remaining six. At the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2008–09 Biathlon World Cup">2008–09 season</a>, Neuner had a substantial drop in her skiing times due to a series of illnesses. However, she recovered and set the fastest course time in 14 of the remaining 18 races from January onwards. In the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2009–10 Biathlon World Cup">2009–10 Olympic season</a>, Neuner again started slowly in December, but came back finishing among the top three fastest skiers in 17 of her 21 races. She had her second best winter in <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2010–11 Biathlon World Cup">2010–11</a> when she set the fastest or second fastest skiing time in 90% of her 21 races.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-22"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Neuner had been a fast cross-country skier from an early age. When she was eight years old, she won the first cross-country skiing competition she entered at her local ski club. At junior level, her lap times at the German Student's Cup were comparable to older or male opponents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parents_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-parents-2">[2]</a></sup> At the age of 15, Neuner managed to set the same skiing times as her coeval male training partners. In preparation for the 2006–07 season, Neuner skied 5,300 kilometres (3,300 mi) in training; she increased the volume to 6,000 kilometres (3,700 mi) for the 2007–08 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-focus_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-focus-24">[24]</a></sup> Because of her ski speed, she has often been able to compensate for one or sometimes two or three shooting errors (a penalty loop is 150 metres (160 yd) long and normally takes 21 to 26 seconds).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-rules-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>During three of her 32 World Cup wins (<a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2007" title="Biathlon World Championships 2007">2007 World Championships</a> pursuit, <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2008" title="Biathlon World Championships 2008">2008 World Championships</a> mass start, and 2009 Ruhpolding pursuit), Neuner skied three additional penalty loops compared to the second-place finisher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wc2_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-wc2-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wc5_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-wc5-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cup13_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-cup13-48">[48]</a></sup> In March 2008, she came in second in the Khanty-Mansiysk mass start race, despite completing five penalty loops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> She also reached third place in the Oberhof pursuit in January 2007 with six missed targets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> At Neuner's first World Cup victory in the individual discipline in January 2010, she compensated for a total time penalty of two minutes on the 15 kilometres (9.3 mi) cross-country course (incurred by two additional shooting errors).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wc14_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-wc14-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Skiing_statistics">Skiing statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Skiing statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Shooting">Shooting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Shooting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Neuner-Trondheim09-2.jpg"><img alt="A woman in multicoloured winter sportswear, wearing a red cap and a jersey with the number 3, holds a rifle in a horizontal position. Her rifle has advertising on its side, while snow falls in the background." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1825" data-file-width="2736" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Neuner-Trondheim09-2.jpg/220px-Neuner-Trondheim09-2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Neuner-Trondheim09-2.jpg/330px-Neuner-Trondheim09-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Neuner-Trondheim09-2.jpg/440px-Neuner-Trondheim09-2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Neuner-Trondheim09-2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Neuner shooting at the World Cup in <a href="/wiki/Trondheim" title="Trondheim">Trondheim</a>, March 2009.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Neuner averaged a career shooting accuracy of 78%. Her career average in the prone position was 88%, while her career average in the standing position was 67%. Her shooting results in the prone position were similar to other top contenders. The standing shoot had long been her weak point and her hit percentage was well below average in the World Cup field, although it had improved considerably in her later seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-24"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>With a 78% accuracy, Neuner had solid shooting results during her <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2005–06 Biathlon World Cup">2005–06 season</a> debut. Her average dropped to 74% in her first complete season in <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2006–07 Biathlon World Cup">2006–07</a>. Neuner won the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2007–08 Biathlon World Cup">2007–08 Biathlon World Cup</a> with a shooting accuracy of 73%, which is the lowest result for an Overall World Cup winner ever and roughly ten per cent below the previous three winners' averages: <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Henkel" title="Andrea Henkel">Andrea Henkel</a> (84%),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kati_Wilhelm" title="Kati Wilhelm">Kati Wilhelm</a> (87%)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Sandrine_Bailly" title="Sandrine Bailly">Sandrine Bailly</a> (81%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> She steadily increased her shooting percentages in the following two seasons with a 76% average in <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2008–09 Biathlon World Cup">2008–09</a>, and her career best results of 82% in the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2009–10 Biathlon World Cup">2009–10 Olympic season</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2010–11 Biathlon World Cup">2010–11 season</a>, she set her career high in the standing position with a 75% accuracy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-25"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Neuner's shooting performances have been a regular topic in the German media. At times she has been reluctant to discuss her shooting in interviews and has said the public's fixation on it contributes to the problem.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pleiten_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-pleiten-42">[42]</a></sup> She has insisted her difficulties in the standing position are not due to technical weaknesses but psychological, and her training results are just as good as the results of her team mates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> She explained in interviews that she had developed a fear of the standing shooting over time, knowing she had to justify herself after the race if she missed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> In 2008, Neuner trained with <a href="/wiki/Bundeswehr" title="Bundeswehr">Bundeswehr</a> shooting coach and former large calibre world champion, Rudi Krenn, and subsequently changed her stance slightly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Since 2009, she has worked with a psychologist, primarily focusing on mental techniques to build her confidence on the shooting range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WSJ_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ-61">[61]</a></sup> Her standing position average has improved from 60% to 75% from 2008 to 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-26"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup> Neuner has been wearing ear plugs during some of the races in order to better concentrate while shooting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-focus_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-focus-24">[24]</a></sup> The individual race, which places a high emphasis on shooting, has traditionally been her worst discipline (each shooting error results in a one-minute time penalty, instead of a penalty loop).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rules_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-rules-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>Neuner has won 6 races (all sprints) with a perfect shooting record: Khanty-Mansiysk sprint in March 2007, <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2011_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_sprint" title="Biathlon World Championships 2011 – Women's sprint">2011 World Championship sprint</a> and 4 sprints in her <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2011–12 Biathlon World Cup">final 2011–12 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cup6_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-cup6-22">[22]</a></sup> She also shot clean on two other occasions, the sprint in Kontiolahti in March 2006, coming in fourth place,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> and the Östersund sprint in December 2008, finishing third.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.C3.B6stersund_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-.C3.B6stersund-44">[44]</a></sup> Her worst shooting performance came in December 2008, with a total of nine shooting errors at the World Cup pursuit in Hochfilzen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> Neuner's costliest shooting occurred during a mass start race in Antholz in January 2009. After 15 clean shots, she was leading by 53.6 seconds before the final shooting, in which she missed all five targets, eventually dropping to sixth place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-disaster_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-disaster-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shooting_statistics">Shooting statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Shooting statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Magdalena_Neuner_Wallgau_2009-2.jpg"><img alt="A blonde woman in casual clothes smilies into the camera. She wears a top with a narrow pattern of black and white strips and stands in a room with traditional Bavarian interior." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3032" data-file-width="2228" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Magdalena_Neuner_Wallgau_2009-2.jpg/170px-Magdalena_Neuner_Wallgau_2009-2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Magdalena_Neuner_Wallgau_2009-2.jpg/255px-Magdalena_Neuner_Wallgau_2009-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Magdalena_Neuner_Wallgau_2009-2.jpg/340px-Magdalena_Neuner_Wallgau_2009-2.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Magdalena_Neuner_Wallgau_2009-2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Neuner in <a href="/wiki/Wallgau" title="Wallgau">Wallgau</a>, Germany, May 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Neuner has lived in <a href="/wiki/Wallgau" title="Wallgau">Wallgau, Bavaria</a>, Germany, a small alpine village of 1,400 people, from birth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-encarta_4-5"><a href="#cite_note-encarta-4">[4]</a></sup> In 2007, she bought her grandmother's house in Wallgau, where she now lives in her own flat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spiegel_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-spiegel-5">[5]</a></sup> Neuner plays the <a href="/wiki/Harp" title="Harp">harp</a> and owns an <a href="/wiki/Enduro" title="Enduro">enduro</a> motorcycle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> She has said she enjoys <a href="/wiki/Mountain_biking" title="Mountain biking">mountain biking</a>, hiking and swimming during the off-season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-finmin_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-finmin-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Neuner had been involved in a nearly two-year relationship with <a href="/wiki/Austrians" title="Austrians">Austrian</a> ski technician and former biathlete Franz Perwein, whom she had met during the 2006 Junior/Youth World Championships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Until the autumn of 2009, she then lived in a relationship with <a href="/wiki/German_Ski_Association" title="German Ski Association">DSV</a> chief biathlon technician Björn Weisheit for 19 months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2009, Neuner confirmed a romantic relationship with Josef Holzer, a school day friend from Wallgau.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> The couple were civilly married in March 2014 and have one daughter, Verena Anna (born 30 May 2014 in <a href="/wiki/Garmisch-Partenkirchen" title="Garmisch-Partenkirchen">Garmisch-Partenkirchen</a>). Their church wedding took place on 17 October 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_the_media">In the media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: In the media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Biathlon is the most popular <a href="/wiki/Winter_sport" title="Winter sport">winter sport</a> in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Each World Cup event is shown live on German television and the January World Cup races in <a href="/wiki/Oberhof,_Germany" title="Oberhof, Germany">Oberhof</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruhpolding" title="Ruhpolding">Ruhpolding</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rasen-Antholz" title="Rasen-Antholz">Antholz</a> are regularly seen by over five million viewers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Following her three world championship titles in 2007, Neuner quickly became one of Germany's most popular female sport stars, often nicknamed "Gold Lena" in the media.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-77">[77]</a></sup> During her first two years in the spotlight she signed several endorsement deals and claimed numerous awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sueddeutsche_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-sueddeutsche-128">[128]</a></sup> Neuner's popularity grew further with her success during the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a>. Her second gold medal win in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_mass_start" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics – Women's mass start">Olympic mass start</a> was seen live by 9.75 million television viewers (a 31.5 per cent market share), the most watched programme of the Games in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Her withdrawal from the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_relay" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics – Women's relay">Olympic relay</a> was one of the dominating stories of the Winter Olympics in Germany, leading to much media speculation whether pulling out had been entirely her decision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> She later received the Fair Play medal of Germany's Olympic Society for setting an example of "team spirit".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed" style="font-size:90%; text-align:center; float:left; margin:1em 1em 1em 0;">
<tr>
<th colspan="2" style="white-space:nowrap; text-align:left;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Sportspersonality_of_the_year" title="German Sportspersonality of the year">German Sportswoman<br/>
of the Year</a> award<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SportlerdesJahres_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-SportlerdesJahres-132">[132]</a></sup>  </th>
