<td style="background:#f7f6a8;">1st</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Neuner won the Biathlon Award, chosen by the national coaches of the World Cup teams, for Female Athlete of the Year in both 2007 and 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-award_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-award-133">[133]</a></sup> and she was awarded the <i>Goldener Ski</i> (Golden Ski), the highest award of the <a href="/wiki/German_Ski_Association" title="German Ski Association">German Ski Association</a> in 2007, 2008 and 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DSV2_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-DSV2-134">[134]</a></sup> The Forum Nordicum, a consortium of journalists form twelve countries, named her Biathlete of the Year in the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2007–08 Biathlon World Cup">2007–08</a> and <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2009–10 Biathlon World Cup">2009–10 seasons</a>, beating out her male counterparts <a href="/wiki/Ole_Einar_Bj%C3%B8rndalen" title="Ole Einar Bjørndalen">Ole Einar Bjørndalen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emil_Hegle_Svendsen" title="Emil Hegle Svendsen">Emil Hegle Svendsen</a> respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nordicum_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-nordicum-135">[135]</a></sup> Neuner was chosen as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Sportspersonality_of_the_year" title="German Sportspersonality of the year">Germany's 2007 Sportswoman of the Year</a> by the country's sports journalists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sportswoman_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-sportswoman-136">[136]</a></sup> The following years, she came in third for the 2008 award and was voted in second place in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> Along with all Olympic medal winners, she received the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silberne_Lorbeerblatt" title="Silberne Lorbeerblatt">Silberne Lorbeerblatt</a></i> (Silver Laurel Leaf) in 2010, the highest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_decoration" title="State decoration">state decoration</a> for athletes in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lorbeer_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-lorbeer-138">[138]</a></sup> In 2011, readers of Germany's top selling newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Bild" title="Bild">Bild</a></i> voted Neuner the seventh greatest German sportsperson of all time,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> and she was again named German Sportswoman of the Year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sportjahres_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-sportjahres-140">[140]</a></sup> Nine months after her retirement, Neuner received Germany's Sportswoman of the Year award for a third time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SportlerdesJahres_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-SportlerdesJahres-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>Neuner's interest in <a href="/wiki/Knitting" title="Knitting">knitting</a> has often been addressed by the German media and she maintains a knitting website, which includes detailed knitting instructions and a "knitting blog". She has stated that she usually takes knitting equipment on her travels during the season and that knitting is a way for her to relax.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> In 2007, Neuner declined an offer to appear nude in the German edition of <i><a href="/wiki/Playboy" title="Playboy">Playboy</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Outside of Germany, she is particularly popular in Russia, where she has a <a href="/wiki/Fan_club" title="Fan club">fan club</a> and from where she has said to receive half of her <a href="/wiki/Fan_mail" title="Fan mail">fan mail</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-focus_24-3"><a href="#cite_note-focus-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> In 2010, Neuner appeared in an advertising campaign for a lingerie line. She explained she tried to use it in a deliberate attempt to correct her media image, after becoming irritated with her public persona of "little sweet Lena".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> She was an ambassador for the <a href="/wiki/2011_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="2011 FIFA Women's World Cup">2011 FIFA Women's World Cup</a> in Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> and a member of the board of trustees for <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>'s bid to host the <a href="/wiki/2018_Winter_Olympics" title="2018 Winter Olympics">2018 Winter Olympics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Record">Record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympic_Games">Olympic Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Olympic Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Neuner-Vancouver-MedalCeremony-cropped.jpg"><img alt="A woman, wearing a predominately yellow and pink jacket and a black cap, stands in front of a blue background, looking to the right. She hold flowers in her hands and has a gold medal around her neck." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="444" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Neuner-Vancouver-MedalCeremony-cropped.jpg/170px-Neuner-Vancouver-MedalCeremony-cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Neuner-Vancouver-MedalCeremony-cropped.jpg/255px-Neuner-Vancouver-MedalCeremony-cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Neuner-Vancouver-MedalCeremony-cropped.jpg/340px-Neuner-Vancouver-MedalCeremony-cropped.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Neuner-Vancouver-MedalCeremony-cropped.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Neuner accepting her Olympic gold medal for the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_pursuit" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics – Women's pursuit">pursuit race</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Neuner has won two gold medals and one silver medal at the Winter Olympic Games. At her only appearance at the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">2010 Winter Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>, Canada, she won gold in the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_pursuit" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics – Women's pursuit">pursuit</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_mass_start" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics – Women's mass start">mass start event</a>. She also claimed silver in the opening <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_at_the_2010_Winter_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_sprint" title="Biathlon at the 2010 Winter Olympics – Women's sprint">sprint</a>. After winning three medals, she decided not to participate in the concluding relay race.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-28"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_championships">World championships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: World championships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Neuner is the most successful female biathlete in the history of <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships" title="Biathlon World Championships">Biathlon World Championships</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goldrausch_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-goldrausch-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> She has won seventeen medals, twelve gold, four silver and one bronze. At her debut during the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2007" title="Biathlon World Championships 2007">2007 World Championships</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rasen-Antholz" title="Rasen-Antholz">Antholz</a>, Italy, Neuner won three titles (sprint, pursuit and relay). One year later at the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2008" title="Biathlon World Championships 2008">2008 World Championships</a> in <a href="/wiki/%C3%96stersund" title="Östersund">Östersund</a>, Sweden, she again claimed three gold medals, winning the mass start, relay and mixed relay events. Neuner did not win a title at the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2009" title="Biathlon World Championships 2009">2009 World Championships</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pyeongchang" title="Pyeongchang">Pyeongchang</a>, South Korea; her best result was the silver medal in the relay event. She won her second mixed relay gold in <a href="/wiki/Khanty-Mansiysk" title="Khanty-Mansiysk">Khanty-Mansiysk</a>, Russia, in 2010. At the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2011" title="Biathlon World Championships 2011">2011 World Championships</a>, she won three more titles (sprint, mass start, relay) and two silver medals (pursuit and mixed relay). At her <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships_2012" title="Biathlon World Championships 2012">final championships</a> in 2012, Neuner won her world titles eleven (sprint) and twelve (relay), as well as her fourth silver (pursuit) and her first bronze medal (mixed relay).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-29"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Cup">World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During her first World Cup season, Neuner only appeared in ten races, finishing 34th in the overall standings. In the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2006–07 Biathlon World Cup">2006–07 season</a>, she became a regular in the German team and ended the season in fourth place. Neuner won the <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Cup" title="Biathlon World Cup">Biathlon World Cup</a> for the first time in <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2007–08 Biathlon World Cup">2007–08</a>; she also won the sprint and mass start disciplines. She finished the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2008–09 Biathlon World Cup">2008–09 season</a> fourth, winning the individual discipline that year. In the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2009–10 Biathlon World Cup">2009–10 season</a>, Neuner won the overall World Cup for a second time; by winning the pursuit and mass start scores as well, she has claimed each World Cup title at least once. In <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2010–11 Biathlon World Cup">2010–11</a>, she won the sprint discipline for a second time and finished fifth in the season ranking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-30"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup> In her final World Cup season in <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Biathlon_World_Cup" title="2011–12 Biathlon World Cup">2011–12</a>, Neuner won her third Overall World Cup title, as well as the sprint discipline.</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Cup_wins">World Cup wins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: World Cup wins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Over the course of seven seasons, Neuner has reached 34 personal World Cup wins. In the history of the <a href="/wiki/International_Biathlon_Union" title="International Biathlon Union">International Biathlon Union</a> she is ranked second behind <a href="/wiki/Magdalena_Forsberg" title="Magdalena Forsberg">Magdalena Forsberg</a> (42), with <a href="/wiki/Uschi_Disl" title="Uschi Disl">Uschi Disl</a> (30) third, for all-time career victories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> In addition, she has won nine relay races and three mixed relay events as part of the German World Cup team. Neuner has often started slowly at the beginning of a winter season and has claimed only three of her individual victories before Christmas. Consequently, 18 of her 47 wins came in the month of March. Geographically most of her wins occurred in <a href="/wiki/Khanty-Mansiysk" title="Khanty-Mansiysk">Khanty-Mansiysk, Russia</a> (10), followed by <a href="/wiki/Rasen-Antholz" title="Rasen-Antholz">Antholz, Italy</a> (6) and <a href="/wiki/Ruhpolding" title="Ruhpolding">Ruhpolding, Germany</a> (6).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-32"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overall_record">Overall record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Overall record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During her seven season on the World Cup tour, Neuner had competed in a total of 175 races, winning 47 of them (a 26.86 win percentage). She has claimed at least one win in each discipline of biathlon and has scored World Cup points in all but three of her races.<sup class="reference" id="ref_WCHg"><a href="#endnote_WCHg">[note b]</a></sup> Neuner has reached a total of 82 World Cup podiums (63 in individual races and 19 in team events). In addition, she has achieved 137 top ten finishes—78.29 per cent of all the races she has entered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-34"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Junior.2FYouth_World_Championships">Junior/Youth World Championships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Junior/Youth World Championships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Neuner has won seven gold and four silver medals at the Biathlon Junior/Youth World Championships. With the exception of the individual discipline, she has won a medal in every race she entered. In 2004, at her first junior world championships in <a href="/wiki/Maurienne" title="Maurienne">Haute Maurienne</a>, France, Neuner won two titles (sprint and relay). One year later, she claimed gold in the sprint race in <a href="/wiki/Kontiolahti" title="Kontiolahti">Kontiolahti</a>, Finland, and in 2006, she again won two titles (pursuit and relay) in <a href="/wiki/Presque_Isle,_Maine" title="Presque Isle, Maine">Presque Isle, Maine</a>, United States. Neuner did not participate in the 2007 event. She returned to the junior world championships in 2008 when they were held in <a href="/wiki/Ruhpolding" title="Ruhpolding">Ruhpolding</a>, Germany, winning two more gold medals (sprint and pursuit).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-36"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></p>

<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Several of Neuner's trophies on temporary display at <a href="/wiki/Wallgau" title="Wallgau">Wallgau</a>'s town hall (from left to right): 2007 German Sportswoman of the Year award, 2007–08 and 2009–10 Overall World Cup crystal globes, 2011 World Championships sprint gold medal</div>
</div>

<p><b>International titles</b></p>
<ul>
<li>Winter Olympic Games – 2 gold medals<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-37"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup>
<ul>
<li>2010: Pursuit, Mass start</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Overall <a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Cup" title="Biathlon World Cup">Biathlon World Cup</a> winner – 2007–08, 2009–10, 2011–2012<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-38"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></li>
<li>Individual World Cup winner – 2008–09<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-39"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></li>
<li>Sprint World Cup winner – 2007–08, 2010–11, 2011–2012<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-40"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></li>
<li>Pursuit World Cup winner – 2009–10<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-41"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></li>
<li>Mass start World Cup winner – 2007–08, 2009–10<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-42"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Biathlon_World_Championships" title="Biathlon World Championships">Biathlon World Championships</a> – 12 gold medals<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-43"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup>
<ul>
<li>2007: Sprint, Pursuit, Relay</li>
<li>2008: Mass start, Relay, Mixed relay</li>
<li>2010: Mixed Relay</li>
<li>2011: Sprint, Mass start, Relay</li>
<li>2012: Sprint, Relay</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Biathlon Junior/Youth World Championships – 7 gold medals<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBUprofile_1-44"><a href="#cite_note-IBUprofile-1">[1]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p><b>Awards</b></p>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Sportspersonality_of_the_year" title="German Sportspersonality of the year">German Sportswoman of the Year</a> – 2007,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sportswoman_136-1"><a href="#cite_note-sportswoman-136">[136]</a></sup> 2011<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sportjahres_140-1"><a href="#cite_note-sportjahres-140">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></li>
<li>Biathlon Award for Female Newcomer of the Year – 2007<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-award_133-1"><a href="#cite_note-award-133">[133]</a></sup></li>
<li>Biathlon Award for Female Athlete of the Year – 2007, 2008<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-award_133-2"><a href="#cite_note-award-133">[133]</a></sup></li>
<li>Goldener Ski of the <a href="/wiki/German_Ski_Association" title="German Ski Association">DSV</a> – 2007, 2008, 2010<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DSV2_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-DSV2-134">[134]</a></sup></li>
<li>Biathlete of the Year of the Forum Nordicum – 2008, 2010<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nordicum_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-nordicum-135">[135]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Silbernes_Lorbeerblatt" title="Silbernes Lorbeerblatt">Silbernes Lorbeerblatt</a> – 2010<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lorbeer_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-lorbeer-138">[138]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Magdalena_Neuner&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="refbegin" style="">
<dl>
<dd><b>a.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_skiinga"><a href="#ref_skiinga"><b><sup>a</sup></b></a></span> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_skiingf"><a href="#ref_skiingf"><b><sup>f</sup></b></a></span> Course times are a measure for a biathlete's skiing performance. They indicate the net skiing time (sum of all lap times), excluding time spent at the shooting range, in the penalty loop or time penalties (individual discipline only).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-handbook_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-handbook-28">[28]</a></sup></dd>
<dd><b>b.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_WCHb"><a href="#ref_WCHb"><b><sup>b</sup></b></a></span> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_WCHg"><a href="#ref_WCHg"><b><sup>g</sup></b></a></span> World Championship and Olympic results are included in Biathlon World Cup scores; gold medals are recognised as World Cup wins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-handbook_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-handbook-28">[28]</a></sup></dd>
<dd><b>c.</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_winnerc"><a href="#ref_winnerc"><b><sup>c</sup></b></a></span> Jirina Pelcová was six months younger when she won the Overall World Cup in 1990 still under the UIPMB, not recognised by the IBU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
</div>
